CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors, such as adenylate cyclase.
CC       Signaling inhibits adenylate cyclase activity (By similarity).
CC       Signaling stimulates TRPM1 channel activity and Ca(2+) uptake.
CC       Required for normal vision. {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:23452348}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131}.
CC       Endoplasmic reticulum membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131}. Golgi
CC       apparatus membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131}. Cell projection,
CC       dendrite {ECO:0000250}. Note=Subject to trafficking from the
CC       endoplasmic reticulum to the Golgi apparatus and then to the cell
CC       membrane.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Detected in melanocytes.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23452348}.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Night blindness, congenital stationary, 1B (CSNB1B)
CC       [MIM:257270]: A non-progressive retinal disorder characterized by
CC       impaired night vision. Congenital stationary night blindness type
CC       1B is an autosomal recessive form associated with a negative
CC       electroretinogram waveform. Patients are night blind from an early
CC       age, and when maximally dark-adapted, they could perceive lights
CC       only with an intensity equal to or slightly dimmer than that
CC       normally detected by the cone system. ERGs in response to single
CC       brief flashes of light have clearly detectable a-waves, which are
CC       derived from photoreceptors, and greatly reduced b-waves, which
CC       are derived from the second-order inner retinal neurons. ERGs in
CC       response to sawtooth flickering light indicate a markedly reduced
CC       on response and a nearly normal OFF response. There is no
CC       subjective delay in the perception of suddenly appearing white vs
CC       black objects on a gray background. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15781871,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17405131, ECO:0000269|PubMed:23714322}.
CC       Note=The disease is caused by mutations affecting the gene
CC       represented in this entry.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RP   X-RAY CRYSTALLOGRAPHY (1.9 ANGSTROMS) OF 42-466 IN COMPLEXES WITH
RP   GABBR1; AGONISTS AND ANTAGONISTS, FUNCTION, SUBUNIT, GLYCOSYLATION AT
RP   ASN-404, AND DISULFIDE BOND.
RX   PubMed=24305054; DOI=10.1038/nature12725;
RA   Geng Y., Bush M., Mosyak L., Wang F., Fan Q.R.;
RT   "Structural mechanism of ligand activation in human GABA(B)
RT   receptor.";
RL   Nature 504:254-259(2013).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Component of a heterodimeric G-protein coupled receptor
CC       for GABA, formed by GABBR1 and GABBR2. Within the heterodimeric
CC       GABA receptor, only GABBR1 seems to bind agonists, while GABBR2
CC       mediates coupling to G proteins. Ligand binding causes a
CC       conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors, such as adenylate cyclase.
CC       Signaling inhibits adenylate cyclase, stimulates phospholipase A2,
CC       activates potassium channels, inactivates voltage-dependent
CC       calcium-channels and modulates inositol phospholipid hydrolysis.
CC       Plays a critical role in the fine-tuning of inhibitory synaptic
CC       transmission. Pre-synaptic GABA receptor inhibits neurotransmitter
CC       release by down-regulating high-voltage activated calcium
CC       channels, whereas postsynaptic GABA receptor decreases neuronal
CC       excitability by activating a prominent inwardly rectifying
CC       potassium (Kir) conductance that underlies the late inhibitory
CC       postsynaptic potentials. Not only implicated in synaptic
CC       inhibition but also in hippocampal long-term potentiation, slow
CC       wave sleep, muscle relaxation and antinociception.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10328880, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18165688,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22660477, ECO:0000269|PubMed:24305054,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9872316}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of GABBR1 and GABBR2. Homodimers may form,
CC       but are inactive. Interacts with ATF4 via its C-terminal region.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10075644, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10773016,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15617512, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18165688,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22660477, ECO:0000269|PubMed:24305054,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9872316}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q9UBS5:GABBR1; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-715469, EBI-724156;
CC       P46459:NSF; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-715469, EBI-712251;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC       Cell junction, synapse, postsynaptic cell membrane; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein. Note=Coexpression of GABBR1 and GABBR2 is
CC       required for GABBR1 maturation and transport to the plasma
CC       membrane. In contrast, GABBR2 does not depend on GABBR1 for
CC       transport to the cell membrane.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Highly expressed in brain, especially in
CC       cerebral cortex, thalamus, hippocampus, frontal, occipital and
CC       temporal lobe, occipital pole and cerebellum, followed by corpus
CC       callosum, caudate nucleus, spinal cord, amygdala and medulla.
CC       Weakly expressed in heart, testis and skeletal muscle.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10087195, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10328880,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10727622}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Alpha-helical parts of the C-terminal intracellular region
CC       mediate heterodimeric interaction with GABBR1.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       GABA-B receptor subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. Signaling activates a
CC       phosphatidylinositol-calcium second messenger system and generates
CC       a calcium-activated chloride current. Plays an important role in
CC       the regulation of synaptic plasticity and the modulation of the
CC       neural network activity. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:7908515,
CC       ECO:0000269|Ref.8}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: The PPXXF motif binds HOMER1, HOMER2 and HOMER3.
CC       Interacts with SIAH1, RYR1, RYR2, ITPR1, SHANK1, SHANK3 and GRASP.
CC       Interacts with NCDN (By similarity). Isoform 2 interacts with
CC       NECAB2 (PubMed:19694902). {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19694902}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q7Z6G3:NECAB2; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-14039683, EBI-950070;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:7908515,
CC       ECO:0000269|Ref.8}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:7908515, ECO:0000269|Ref.8}.

RP   INTERACTION WITH ARRB1.
RX   PubMed=17623778; DOI=10.1242/jcs.03469;
RA   Bouschet T., Martin S., Kanamarlapudi V., Mundell S., Henley J.M.;
RT   "The calcium-sensing receptor changes cell shape via a beta-arrestin-1
RT   ARNO ARF6 ELMO protein network.";
RL   J. Cell Sci. 120:2489-2497(2007).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein-coupled receptor that senses changes in the
CC       extracellular concentration of calcium ions and plays a key role
CC       in maintaining calcium homeostasis (PubMed:7816802). Senses
CC       fluctuations in the circulating calcium concentration and
CC       modulates the production of parathyroid hormone (PTH) in
CC       parathyroid glands (By similarity). The activity of this receptor
CC       is mediated by a G-protein that activates a phosphatidylinositol-
CC       calcium second messenger system (By similarity). The G-protein-
CC       coupled receptor activity is activated by a co-agonist mechanism:
CC       aromatic amino acids, such as Trp or Phe, act concertedly with
CC       divalent cations, such as calcium or magnesium, to achieve full
CC       receptor activation (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180, ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q9QY96}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: In resting state, adopts an open conformation,
CC       anion-binding promoting the inactive configuration. Upon aromatic
CC       amino acid-binding, the groove in the extracellular venus flytrap
CC       module is closed, thereby inducing the formation of a novel
CC       homodimer interface between subunits. Calcium ions stabilize the
CC       active state by enhancing homodimer interactions between membrane-
CC       proximal domains to fully activate the receptor.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked (By similarity). Interacts
CC       with VCP and RNF19A (By similarity). Interacts with ARRB1
CC       (PubMed:17623778). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17623778}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The extracellular regions of the homodimer interact in a
CC       side-by-side fashion while facing opposite directions. Each
CC       extracellular region consists of three domains, LB1 (ligand-
CC       binding 1), LB2 and CR (cysteine-rich). The two lobe-shaped
CC       domains LB1 and LB2 form a venus flytrap module. In the inactive
CC       configuration, the venus flytrap modules of both protomers are in
CC       the open conformation associated with the resting state (open-
CC       open) and the interdomain cleft is empty. In addition, each
CC       protomer contains three anions, which reinforce the inactive
CC       conformation, and one calcium ion. In the active configuration,
CC       both protomers of extracellular regions have the closed
CC       conformation associated with agonist-binding (closed-closed). The
CC       ligand-binding cleft of each protomer is solely occupied by an
CC       aromatic amino-acid. Calcium is bound at four novel sites,
CC       including one at the homodimer interface. Agonist-binding induces
CC       large conformational changes within the extracellular region
CC       homodimer: first, the venus flytrap module of each protomer
CC       undergoes domain closure. Second, the LB2 regions of the two
CC       protomers approach each other, resulting in an expansion of the
CC       homodimer interactions involving LB2 domains. Third, the CR
CC       regions of the two subunits interact to form a large homodimer
CC       interface that is unique to the active state. The CR regions are
CC       brought into close contact by the motion involving LB2 since the
CC       two domains are rigidly associated within each subunit.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by RNF19A; which induces proteasomal
CC       degradation. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41180}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. Signaling inhibits adenylate
CC       cyclase activity.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with PICK1. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11122333}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Prominent expression in olfactory bulb,
CC       pontine gray, lateral reticular nucleus of the thalamus, and
CC       piriform cortex. Less abundant expression incerebral cortex,
CC       hippocampus, cerebellum, and mammillary body.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10821630,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8824309}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8824309};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8824309}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the neurons of the larval CNS
CC       from the beginning of the first until the third instar. Expression
CC       in the third-instar larval CNS is restricted to a discrete number
CC       of somas and projections in the brain lobes and in the ventral
CC       ganglion. In the ventral nerve cord, expression is detected both
CC       in somas and projections. Expressed in the antennal lobes, the
CC       optic lobes, the central complex and the median bundle in the
CC       adult CNS. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11536189}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed in the CNS of the late embryo.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8824309}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RT   "The consensus coding sequences of human breast and colorectal

RL   Science 314:268-274(2006).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. Signaling activates a
CC       phosphatidylinositol-calcium second messenger system. May
CC       participate in the central action of glutamate in the CNS, such as
CC       long-term potentiation in the hippocampus and long-term depression
CC       in the cerebellum. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24603153,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:7476890}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Signaling is inhibited by the antagonist
CC       LY341495. The LY341495 binding site partially overlaps with the
CC       glutamate binding site. Signaling is also inhibited by synthetic
CC       allosteric regulators, such as FITM (4-fluoro-N-(4-(6-
CC       (isopropylamino)pyrimidin-4-yl)thiazol-2-yl)-N-methylbenzamide)
CC       that bind in a pocket between the transmembrane helices.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24603153}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked. The PPXXF motif binds
CC       HOMER1, HOMER2 and HOMER3. Interacts with SIAH1, RYR1, RYR2,
CC       ITPR1, SHANK1, SHANK3 and GRASP (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P52294:KPNA1; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-8527352, EBI-358383;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24603153};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24603153}.
CC   -!- ALTERNATIVE PRODUCTS:
CC       Event=Alternative splicing; Named isoforms=3;
CC       Name=Alpha;
CC         IsoId=Q13255-1; Sequence=Displayed;
CC       Name=Beta;
CC         IsoId=Q13255-2; Sequence=VSP_002024, VSP_002025;
CC         Note=Ref.1 (AAA87844) sequence is in conflict in position:
CC         896:T->S. Ref.1 (AAA87844) sequence is in conflict in position:
CC         904:V->A. {ECO:0000305};
CC       Name=3;
CC         IsoId=Q13255-3; Sequence=VSP_055127, VSP_055128;
CC         Note=No experimental confirmation available.;
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Detected in brain.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Spinocerebellar ataxia, autosomal recessive, 13 (SCAR13)
CC       [MIM:614831]: Spinocerebellar ataxia is a clinically and
CC       genetically heterogeneous group of cerebellar disorders. Patients
CC       show progressive incoordination of gait and often poor
CC       coordination of hands, speech and eye movements, due to
CC       degeneration of the cerebellum with variable involvement of the
CC       brainstem and spinal cord. SCAR13 is characterized by delayed
CC       psychomotor development beginning in infancy. Affected individuals
CC       show mild to profound mental retardation with poor or absent
CC       speech as well as gait and stance ataxia and hyperreflexia.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:22901947}. Note=The disease is caused by
CC       mutations affecting the gene represented in this entry.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors, such as adenylate cyclase.
CC       Signaling inhibits adenylate cyclase activity. May mediate
CC       suppression of neurotransmission or may be involved in
CC       synaptogenesis or synaptic stabilization.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18297054, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22300836,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:23129762, ECO:0000269|PubMed:7620613}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with GRASP (By similarity). Interacts with
CC       HTR2A. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18297054,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22300836, ECO:0000269|PubMed:23129762}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q58DX5:NAALADL2; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-10232876, EBI-10178964;
CC       Q9UMX0-2:UBQLN1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-10232876, EBI-10173939;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC       Cell junction, synapse {ECO:0000250}. Cell projection, dendrite
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Detected in brain cortex (at protein level).
CC       Widely expressed in different regions of the adult brain as well
CC       as in fetal brain. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18297054}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. Signaling inhibits adenylate
CC       cyclase activity. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8840013}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Putative taste receptor. TAS1R1/TAS1R3 responds to the
CC       umami taste stimulus (the taste of monosodium glutamate).
CC       TAS1R2/TAS1R3 recognizes diverse natural and synthetic sweeteners.
CC       TAS1R3 is essential for the recognition and response to the

CC       within and between species can significantly influence the
CC       selectivity and specificity of taste responses (By similarity).

CC   -!- FUNCTION: May be involved in early development in cAMP sensing and
CC       subsequent chemotactic response. Probable receptor of GABA and
CC       glutamate, leading respectively to the induction or inhibition of
CC       SDF-2 formation. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16672332,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16527814};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16527814}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed throughout development. Expression
CC       is very low in vegetative cells and starts to accumulate in the
CC       first 2 hours after the initiation of development. It reaches a
CC       peak at 4 hours and then declines. However, a slightly larger
CC       transcript accumulates after 10 hours and remains until 22 hours
CC       of development. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16527814,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16672332, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Down-regulated by growth on bacteria.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18559084}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Cells grow faster, reach higher densities,
CC       exhibit delayed aggregates formation upon starvation and altered
CC       chemotaxis toward cAMP. Cells do not produce SDF-2 in response to
CC       GABA. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16527814, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16672332}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: May act during the development and be a negative
CC       regulator. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.
CC       Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}; Multi-pass membrane
CC       protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}. Endoplasmic reticulum
CC       membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}. Golgi apparatus membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}. Nucleus envelope
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}. Note=May also localize to internal
CC       membranes.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed throughout growth and development
CC       with a strong increase in early and late development.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Cells show precocious development.
CC       Alterations are also noted at the slug stage and in spore
CC       formation. Slugs are longer and break apart several times on their
CC       way to culmination forming smaller but proportionate fruiting
CC       bodies. Spores from fruiting bodies are malformed and less viable,
CC       although the spore differentiation factors are synthesized and
CC       sensed normally. Mutant completes development 6 hours earlier.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17501984}.

CC       lipoprotein family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC       coupled receptor 3 family. GABA-B receptor subfamily.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Putative taste receptor. TAS1R1/TAS1R3 responds to the
CC       umami taste stimulus (the taste of monosodium glutamate).
CC       TAS1R2/TAS1R3 recognizes diverse natural and synthetic sweeteners.
CC       TAS1R3 is essential for the recognition and response to the
CC       disaccharide trehalose (By similarity). Sequence differences
CC       within and between species can significantly influence the
CC       selectivity and specificity of taste responses. {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11917125, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12892531}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Forms homodimers or heterodimers with TAS1R1 and TAS1R2.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       TAS1R subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC       - Issue 55 of February 2005;

CC       umami taste stimulus (the taste of monosodium glutamate). Sequence
CC       differences within and between species can significantly influence
CC       the selectivity and specificity of taste responses.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11917125}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor activated by amino acids with a preference for
CC       basic amino acids such as L-Lys, L-Arg and L-ornithine but also by
CC       small and polar amino acids. The L-alpha amino acids respond is
CC       augmented by divalent cations Ca(2+) and Mg(2+). Activated by
CC       extracellular calcium and osteocalcin. Seems to act through a
CC       G(q)/G(11) and G(i)-coupled pathway. Mediates the non-genomic
CC       effects of androgens in multiple tissue. May coordinate
CC       nutritional and hormonal anabolic signals through the sensing of
CC       extracellular amino acids, osteocalcin, divalent ions and its
CC       responsiveness to anabolic steroids. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15576628,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16199532, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19050760,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20947496}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15816861}.

RP   INTERACTION WITH EGFR, AND PHOSPHORYLATION AT TYR-317; TYR-320;
RP   TYR-347 AND TYR-350 BY EGFR.
RX   PubMed=25311788; DOI=10.1186/1476-4598-13-233;
RA   Lin X., Zhong S., Ye X., Liao Y., Yao F., Yang X., Sun B., Zhang J.,
RA   Li Q., Gao Y., Wang Y., Liu J., Han B., Chin Y.E., Zhou B.P., Deng J.;
RT   "EGFR phosphorylates and inhibits lung tumor suppressor GPRC5A in lung
RT   cancer.";
RL   Mol. Cancer 13:233-233(2014).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Orphan receptor. Could be involved in modulating
CC       differentiation and maintaining homeostasis of epithelial cells.
CC       This retinoic acid-inducible GPCR provide evidence for a possible
CC       interaction between retinoid and G-protein signaling pathways.
CC       Functions as a negative modulator of EGFR signaling (By
CC       similarity). May act as a lung tumor suppressor (PubMed:18000218).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q8BHL4, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18000218}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts (via its transmembrane domain) with EGFR.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25311788}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9857033};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}. Cytoplasmic vesicle
CC       membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9857033}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000255}. Note=Localized in perinuclear vesicles, probably
CC       Golgi-associated vesicles. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:18000218}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed at high level in fetal and adult
CC       lung tissues but repressed in most human lung cancers
CC       (PubMed:9857033, PubMed:18000218). Constitutively expressed in
CC       fetal kidney and adult placenta, kidney, prostate, testis, ovary,
CC       small intestine, colon, stomach, and spinal chord at low to
CC       moderate levels. Not detectable in fetal heart, brain, and liver
CC       and adult heart, brain, liver, skeletal muscle, pancreas, spleen,
CC       thymus, and peripheral leukocytes. According to PubMed:10783259,
CC       expressed at low but detectable level in pancreas and heart.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10783259, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10945465,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18000218, ECO:0000269|PubMed:9857033}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: By all-trans retinoic acid (ATRA).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9857033}.
CC   -!- PTM: Phosphorylated in two conserved double-tyrosine motifs, TYR-
CC       317/TYR-320 and TYR-347/TYR-350, by EGFR; leading to inactivation
CC       of the tumor suppressive function of GPRC5A in lung cancer cells.
CC       TYR-317 and TYR-320 are the preferred residues responsible for
CC       EGFR-mediated GPRC5A phosphorylation.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25311788}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RP   ALLELIC VARIATION RESPONSE TO SWEETENERS.
RC   STRAIN=129/J, and C57BL/ByJ;
RX   PubMed=14999080; DOI=10.1523/JNEUROSCI.4439-03.2004;
RA   Inoue M., Reed D.R., Li X., Tordoff M.G., Beauchamp G.K.,
RA   Bachmanov A.A.;
RT   "Allelic variation of the Tas1r3 taste receptor gene selectively
RT   affects behavioral and neural taste responses to sweeteners in the F2
RT   hybrids between C57BL/6ByJ and 129P3/J mice.";
RL   J. Neurosci. 24:2296-2303(2004).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Putative taste receptor. TAS1R1/TAS1R3 responds to the
CC       umami taste stimulus (the taste of monosodium glutamate) and also
CC       to most of the 20 standard L-amino acids, but not to their D-
CC       enantiomers or other compounds. TAS1R2/TAS1R3 recognizes diverse
CC       natural and synthetic sweeteners. TAS1R3 is essential for the
CC       recognition and response to the disaccharide trehalose. Sequence
CC       differences within and between species can significantly influence
CC       the selectivity and specificity of taste responses.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11894099, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12892531}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Forms homodimers or heterodimers with TAS1R1 and TAS1R2.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in circumvallate, foliate and
CC       fungiform taste papillae as well as in taste buds on the palate.
CC       Also expressed in testis. Not expressed in brain, heart, kidney,
CC       liver or spleen. The topographic distribution in various taste
CC       papillae is different from those of other T1R members.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11319557, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11322794,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11326277, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11331418}.
CC   -!- PTM: The Thr-60 variant is predicted to introduce a novel N-linked
CC       glycosylation site at Asn-58. The addition of even a short
CC       carbohydrate group at Asn-58 is predicted to disrupt one of the
CC       contact surfaces required for stability of a dimer. Therefore a
CC       Thr-60 variant N-glycosylated at Asn-58 is predicted to be
CC       precluded from forming homodimers or heterodimers.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       TAS1R subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Putative taste receptor. TAS1R1/TAS1R3 responds to the
CC       umami taste stimulus (the taste of monosodium glutamate) and also
CC       to most of the 20 standard L-amino acids, but not to their D-
CC       enantiomers or other compounds. Sequence differences within and
CC       between species can significantly influence the selectivity and
CC       specificity of taste responses. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11894099}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Forms heterodimers with TAS1R3.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed strongly only in fungiform papillae.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11319557}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       TAS1R subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Olfactory receptor that is activated by amino acids that
CC       act as potent odorants in fish. Most highly activated by basic
CC       amino acids such as L-lysine and L-arginine.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10433261}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in olfactory epithelium. Also
CC       expressed in gills, tongue, lips and palatal organ. Not expressed
CC       in brain, kidney, liver, muscle, intestine, ovary and skin. In
CC       olfactory epithelium, it is widely expressed over the apical and
CC       medial portions of the olfactory sensory neurons, regions that
CC       contain olfactory neurons. Expressed in external epithelia, which
CC       contains taste buds and solitary chemosensory cells. On gill
CC       rakers, it is widely expressed in the surface epithelium, but
CC       excluded from taste buds. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10433261}.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RA   Blein S., Ginham R., Uhrin D., Smith B.O., Soares D.C., Veltel S.,

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Component of a heterodimeric G-protein coupled receptor
CC       for GABA, formed by GABBR1 and GABBR2. Within the heterodimeric
CC       GABA receptor, only GABBR1 seems to bind agonists, while GABBR2
CC       mediates coupling to G proteins. Ligand binding causes a
CC       conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors, such as adenylate cyclase.
CC       Signaling inhibits adenylate cyclase, stimulates phospholipase A2,
CC       activates potassium channels, inactivates voltage-dependent
CC       calcium-channels and modulates inositol phospholipid hydrolysis.
CC       Calcium is required for high affinity binding to GABA. Plays a
CC       critical role in the fine-tuning of inhibitory synaptic
CC       transmission. Pre-synaptic GABA receptor inhibits neurotransmitter
CC       release by down-regulating high-voltage activated calcium
CC       channels, whereas postsynaptic GABA receptor decreases neuronal
CC       excitability by activating a prominent inwardly rectifying
CC       potassium (Kir) conductance that underlies the late inhibitory
CC       postsynaptic potentials. Not only implicated in synaptic
CC       inhibition but also in hippocampal long-term potentiation, slow
CC       wave sleep, muscle relaxation and antinociception.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9069281}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer of GABBR1 and GABBR2. Homodimers may form,
CC       but are inactive. Interacts with the leucine zipper of the C-
CC       terminal bZIP domain of ATF4 via its C-terminal region. Interacts
CC       with JAKMIP1. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10075644,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10924501, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14718537,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9872744}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       O88871:Gabbr2; NbExp=8; IntAct=EBI-7090268, EBI-7090239;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC       Cell junction, synapse, postsynaptic cell membrane; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein. Cell projection, dendrite. Note=Coexpression of
CC       GABBR1 and GABBR2 is required for GABBR1 maturation and transport
CC       to the plasma membrane. Colocalizes with ATF4 in hippocampal
CC       neuron dendritic membranes.

CC         IsoId=Q9Z0U4-5; Sequence=VSP_002044, VSP_002045, VSP_002046;
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Isoform 1A, isoform 1B and isoform 1C are
CC       expressed in testis, stomach, spinal cord and brain including
CC       cerebral cortical layers, pyramidal cell layers of the
CC       hippocampus, granular cell layers of the dentate gyrus, basal
CC       ganglia, cerebellum (predominantly in Purkinje cells followed by
CC       granular layer). Isoform 1B is also expressed in kidney and liver.
CC       Isoform 1D is expressed in forebrain, cerebellum, eye, kidney, and
CC       urinary bladder. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10658574,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9069281, ECO:0000269|PubMed:9875211}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Alpha-helical parts of the C-terminal intracellular region
CC       mediate heterodimeric interaction with GABBR2. The linker region
CC       between the transmembrane domain 3 (TM3) and the transmembrane
CC       domain 4 (TM4) probably plays a role in the specificity for G-
CC       protein coupling.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor 3 family.
CC       GABA-B receptor subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.
